55ğ“€´To Sherlock Holmes she is always _the_ woman. I have seldom heard him
56ğ“€´mention her under any other name. In his eyes she eclipses and
57ğ“€´predominates the whole of her sex. It was not that he felt any emotion
58ğ“€´akin to love for Irene Adler. All emotions, and that one particularly,
59ğ“€´were abhorrent to his cold, precise but admirably balanced mind. He
60ğ“€´was, I take it, the most perfect reasoning and observing machine that
61ğ“€´the world has seen, but as a lover he would have placed himself in a
62ğ“€´false position. He never spoke of the softer passions, save with a gibe
63ğ“€´and a sneer. They were admirable things for the observerâ€”excellent for
64ğ“€´drawing the veil from menâ€™s motives and actions. But for the trained
65ğ“€´reasoner to admit such intrusions into his own delicate and finely
66ğ“€´adjusted temperament was to introduce a distracting factor which might
67ğ“€´throw a doubt upon all his mental results. Grit in a sensitive
68ğ“€´instrument, or a crack in one of his own high-power lenses, would not
69ğ“€´be more disturbing than a strong emotion in a nature such as his. And
70ğ“€´yet there was but one woman to him, and that woman was the late Irene
71ğ“€´Adler, of dubious and questionable memory.
72ğ“€´
73ğ“€´I had seen little of Holmes lately. My marriage had drifted us away

75ğ“€´interests which rise up around the man who first finds himself master

78ğ“€´soul, remained in our lodgings in Baker Street, buried among his old
79ğ“€´books, and alternating from week to week between cocaine and ambition,
80ğ“€´the drowsiness of the drug, and the fierce energy of his own keen
81ğ“€´nature. He was still, as ever, deeply attracted by the study of crime,
82ğ“€´and occupied his immense faculties and extraordinary powers of
83ğ“€´observation in following out those clues, and clearing up those
84ğ“€´mysteries which had been abandoned as hopeless by the official police.
